Sequences from out-group species were used to detect cases of selective loss of orthologs. The A-B sequence pairs were eliminated if either sequence A or sequence B scored higher to an out-group sequence than to each other. Additionally, orthologs based on in-paralogs were clustered together with each remaining pair of potential orthologs. Overlapping clusters were resolved by a set of rules adopted from Inparanoid. The parameters used were the defaults of a cutoff bit score of 50, in-paralog confidence cutoff of 0.05 and group overlap of 0.5, where homologs were grouped if they were similar enough to each other. Other parameters used were a cutoff of 0.5 for total sequence overlaps and 0.25 for segment overlaps. Additional details and specific species analyzed are presented in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.740#MOESM3">Supplementary Note</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec25">Transcriptome analysis.</h3><p>Total RNA was isolated from mature <i>F. vesca</i> Hawaii-4 (accession PI551572) organs subjected to a wide array of treatment conditions, including stress, light, growth regulators and pharmacological treatments, as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Folta, K.M. et al. A.transcript accounting from diverse tissues of a cultivated strawberry. Plant Genome 3, 90â105 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3009">51</a></sup>. Normalized pools were converted to full-length enriched cDNA using the SMART method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Zhu, Y.Y., Machleder, E.M., Chenchik, A., Li, R. &amp; Siebert, P.D. Reverse transcriptase template switching: a SMART approach for full-length cDNA library construction. Biotechniques 30, 892â897 (2001)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3013">52</a></sup> and sequenced using Illumina protocols. Reads were filtered and mapped to the <i>F. vesca</i> genome using HashMatch (see <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="section anchor" href="/articles/ng.740#Sec19">URLs</a>) and Supersplat<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Bryant, D.W. Jr., Shen, R., Priest, H.D., Wong, W.K. &amp; Mockler, T.C. Supersplat-spliced RNA-seq alignment. Bioinformatics 26, 1500â1505 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3024">53</a></sup>. Data are available in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive under accession SRA026313.1. Transcript reads used for gene annotation were sequenced using 454, from RNA isolated specifically from fruit (developmental stages from initial buds to overripe) and roots (including root tips, roots and crown root initials). Data are available in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive under accession <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRA026350.1">SRA026350.1</a>. Overrepresented gene ontology categories were determined as described in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.740#MOESM3">Supplementary Note</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec26">Multiple genome alignment.</h3><p>Genomes from other species were pairwise compared to the <i>F. vesca</i> sequence using MUMmer3, option promer, using the <i>F. vesca</i> genome as the first member of the pair. Results were then merged based on overlaps between matched regions in the anchor genome. Details on genomes used and additional parameters of the test are presented in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.740#MOESM3">Supplementary Note</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec27">Analysis of large duplications in the <i>Fragaria vesca</i> genome.</h3><p>A comparison of the <i>F. vesca</i> genome was made against itself using MUMmer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3070">47</a></sup> version 3.22 at the nucleotide level (nucmer). Two approaches were implemented. The first measured matches by MUMmer excluding whole contig self-matches. The second used BOWTIE to match Illumina reads against contigs and for quantifying unique hits. Details are presented in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.740#MOESM3">Supplementary Note</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec28">Gene ontology annotation.</h3><p>A functional annotation pipeline provided gene ontology assignments to 25,051 genes. Peptide sequences were analyzed through Interproscan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Hunter, S. et al. InterPro: the integrative protein signature database. Nucleic Acids Res. 37, D211âD215 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3085">54</a></sup>, followed by SignalP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Emanuelsson, O., Brunak, S., von Heijne, G. &amp; Nielsen, H. Locating proteins in the cell using TargetP, SignalP and related tools. Nat. Protoc. 2, 953â971 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3089">55</a></sup>, Predotar<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Small, I., Peeters, N., Legeai, F. &amp; Lurin, C. Predotar: A tool for rapidly screening proteomes for N-terminal targeting sequences. Proteomics 4, 1581â1590 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3093">56</a></sup> and TMHMM<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Krogh, A., Larsson, B., von Heijne, G. &amp; Sonnhammer, E.L.L. Predicting transmembrane protein topology with a hidden Markov model: application to complete genomes. J. Mol. Biol. 305, 567â580 (2001)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3097">57</a></sup>. Additional details are presented in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.740#MOESM3">Supplementary Note</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec29">Identification of disease resistance genes.</h3><p>Putative disease resistance genes such as pathogenesis-related (PR) proteins and biosynthesis and/or response genes associated with jasmonic acid, salicylic acid and nitric acid were identified using a keyword search in the NCBI database, with priority given to results from the Rosaceae family. Sequences from this search were used to interrogate the <i>F. vesca</i> genome using BLASTx. Hits with an <i>e</i> value &lt;10<sup>7</sup>, <i>a</i> score &gt; 150 and &gt;50% identity are presented.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec30">Transcription factor identification.</h3><p>Protein sequences for plant transcription factors were downloaded from the Peking University Plant Transcription Factor Databases repository. A Reciprocal Best Hit (RBH) approach was used to identify and classify putative strawberry transcription factors by BLASTx<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Altschul, S.F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E.W. &amp; Lipman, D.J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403â410 (1990)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3131">58</a></sup> using a threshold cut off of 10 Ã 10<sup>â20</sup>. RBHs were extracted by parsing BLASTx tabular outputs using a PERL script. Protein family motifs, detected by InterproScan version 4.4 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Zdobnov, E.M. &amp; Apweiler, R. InterProScan-an integration platform for the signature-recognition methods in InterPro. Bioinformatics 17, 847â848 (2001)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3136">59</a>), were used to confirm (but not exclude) putative strawberry transcription factors. Protein sequence alignments were performed using ClustalW version 2.0.11<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Larkin, M.A. et al. Clustal W and Clustal X version 2.0. Bioinformatics 23, 2947â2948 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3140">60</a></sup>. This conservative approach revealed 1,616 transcription factor genes, which is more than <i>Vitis</i> (1,403) but less than <i>Arabidopsis</i> (1,856) (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.740#MOESM3">Supplementary Table 17</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec31">Angiosperm phylogeny based on 154 protein-coding genes.</h3><p>Putative single-copy genes were retrieved from ten angiosperm genomes using the GeneTrees database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Tian, Y. &amp; Dickerman, A.W. GeneTrees: a phylogenomics resource for prokaryotes. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, D328âD331 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3163">61</a></sup> and subsequently available genomes. Homologous protein sequences were trimmed to eliminate non-conserved terminal regions and aligned with MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Edgar, R.C. MUSCLE: a multiple sequence alignment method with reduced time and space complexity. BMC Bioinformatics 5, 1â19 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3167">62</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Edgar, R.C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â1797 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3170">63</a></sup>, and trees were inferred for each gene family using RAxML 2.3 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Stamatakis, A., Ludwig, T. &amp; Meier, H. RAxML-III: a fast program for maximum likelihood-based inference of large phylogenetic trees. Bioinformatics 21, 456â463 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3173">64</a>). Screening for phylogenetic coherence and the presence of paralogs (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.740#MOESM3">Supplementary Note</a>) resulted in 154 orthologous gene families missing members from at most two genomes. These families were realigned (MUSCLE) and poorly aligned regions were filtered with Gblocks<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Talavera, G. &amp; Castresana, J. Improvement of phylogenies after removing divergent and ambiguously aligned blocks from protein sequence alignments. Syst. Biol. 56, 564â577 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3180">65</a></sup>. Filtered alignments were concatenated to a matrix of 68,526 characters and analyzed with RAxML using GTR and gamma-distributed rate variation. The approximately unbiased test<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Shimodaira, H. An approximately unbiased test of phylogenetic tree selection. Syst. Biol. 51, 492â508 (2002)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3185">35</a></sup>, as implemented in the program CONSEL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Shimodaira, H. &amp; Hasegawa, M. CONSEL: for assessing the confidence of phylogenetic tree selection. Bioinformatics 17, 1246â1247 (2001)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3189">66</a></sup>, was used to evaluate our placement of poplar, the 'poplar-Brassicales topology', against the widely accepted 'Fabidae topology'<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Wang, H. et al. Rosid radiation and the rapid rise of Angiosperm-dominated forests. Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA 106, 3853â3858 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.740#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d43998e3193">37</a></sup>.</p><p>Sources for the protein or nucleotide datasets, individual sequence identifiers with subsequence ranges, output files from tree analyses and a detailed work flow are available at <a href="http://staff.vbi.vt.edu/allan/StrawberryPhylogenomics">http://staff.vbi.vt.edu/allan/StrawberryPhylogenomics</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec32">Accession codes.</h3><p>This whole-genome shotgun project has been deposited at DDBJ, EMBL and GenBank under the project accession <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=AEMH00000000">AEMH00000000</a>. Sequence reads have been deposited to the short-read archive under the following notation: <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRA020125">SRA020125</a> contains 454-generated genomic reads, <a href="http://trace.ddbj.nig.ac.jp/DRASearch/getSubmissionDetail?query=SRA026313">SRA026313</a> contains Illumina RNA-seq and genomic data and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRA026350">SRA026350</a> contains 454 transcriptome reads.</p></div></div></section>
